Key Takeaway
The debate over whether particles and verbs are universal or particular in placement hinges on whether their wad' is for a general concept that becomes specified in usage or for a particular instance directly.

The Three Types of Linguistic Placement (Wad')
Author classifies three types of wad' and explains the impossibility of the fourth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which of the three types of wad' (general-for-specific, specific-for-specific, general-for-general) a given word belongs to, and explain why specific-for-general is impossible.

Core Idea
Linguistic placement has only three possible types; the fourth is logically impossible.

In this passage, the commentator elaborates on al-Aḍud's classification of linguistic assignment (wad') into three types. Understanding this classification is essential for analyzing how words carry meaning in Islamic legal theory and logic. We will walk through the three types and the logical impossibility of a fourth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base terms
Locate 'wad'' (placement), 'mawdu' lahu' (assigned meaning), and the classification in the text. The passage distinguishes between general and specific in both the tool and the object.
The tool is the concept used by the assigner; the object is what the word points to.
2
List the three types from the passage
Find the three divisions: (1) wad' 'amm li mawdu' lahu khass (general-for-specific), (2) wad' khass li mawdu' lahu khass (proper nouns), (3) wad' 'amm li mawdu' lahu 'amm (e.g., 'rajul' for the genus man).
The text calls the third type 'placing a word like 'rajul' for its meaning'.
3
Examine the example of proper nouns
The commentator says proper nouns ('alam) are specific-for-specific: the word is assigned to a specific individual with a specific meaning. Contrast this with demonstratives and pronouns.
4
Understand why specific-for-general is impossible
The commentator states that a particular cannot serve as a tool to observe a universal. This is a logical principle: the tool must be more general than the object. Absorb the reasoning.
This prevents the fourth type: wad' khass li mawdu' lahu 'amm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَيْ : لِمُشَخَصِ بِاعْتِبَارِ تَعَقْلِهِ (١) لَا بِخُصُوصِهِ، بَلْ بِأَمْرٍ عَامٌ كَالإِشَارَةِ فِي اسْمِ الإِشَارَةِ، وَالتَّكَلُّمِ أَوِ الخِطَابِ فِي الضَّمِيرِ، وَيُسَمَّى هَذَا الوَضْعُ: «وَضْعاً عَامَّا لِمَوْضُوعِ لَهُ خَاصٌ»، بِخِلَافِ وَضْعِ العَلَمِ، فَإِنَّهُ خَاصٌ لِخَاصٌ لَكِنْ يُسْتَثْنَى مِنَ المَعَارِفِ مَا كَانَ مِنْهَا فِي قُوَّةِ النَّكِرَةِ كَـ : المُعَرَّفِ بِلَامِ الحَقِيقَةِ، أَوِ العَهْدِ حَيْثُ يَكُونُ المَعْهُودُ غَيْرَ مُعَيَّنِ، وَالمُعَرَّفِ بالإِضَافَةِ الجِنْسِيَّةِ، وَالمَوْصُولِ الَّذِي يُرَادُ بِهِ الجِنْسُ ، فَإِنَّهَا كُلِّيَّاتٌ قَطعاً ؛ انْظُرْ رِسَالَةِ العَضُدِ». (٣) - الثَّالِثُ : الجُزْنِيُّ بِالمَعْنَى السَّابِقِ يُسَمَّى : «الجُزْئِيَّ الحَقِيقِيَّ»؛ لِأَنَّ جُزْئِيَّتَهُ بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَى ذَاتِهِ . قصارة. قوله : (بِاعْتِبَارِ تَعَقلِهِ) معناه : أنَّ الواضع يعتبر أمراً مشتركاً بين جزئيات مشخصات ك: التكلم، ويقول مثلاً : هذا اللفظ موضوع لكلِّ واحدٍ من هذه الجزئيات المشخّصات بخصوصه بحيث لا يفهم منه إلَّا واحدٌ بخصوصه دون القدر المشترك، وإنما يتعقل ذلك القدر المشترك ليكون آلة للوضع لتلك الجزئيات، لا لأنَّه هو الموضوع له، هذا معنى كون الوضع عاما والموضوع له خاصا قال السَّيِّد في حواشي شرح المطالع : ومن لم يعرف الوضع العام لموضوع له خاص وقع في حيص بيص؛ أي: ضيق وشدة. قوله : (بِخِلَافِ وَضْعِ العَلَمِ) هذا هو القسم الثاني مِنَ الأقسام الثَّلاثة التي قسم العضدُ في رسالته اللفظ الموضوع إليها ؛ والأوَّل: وضع عام لموضوع له خاص وهو الذي تقدم، والثالث : وضع لفظة رجل لمعناه؛ أي: ما وضع لأمر عام وضعاً عاماً ، وأمَّا عكس الأول وهو وضع خاص لعام فمحال الوجود؛ إذ لا يكون الجزئي آلة لملاحظة الكلّيّ . قوله : (لَكِنْ يُسْتَثْنَى) هذا المستثنى هو داخل في القسم الثَّالث الذي ذكرناه، وهو وضع عام لموضوع له عام. :قوله :(كَـ : المُعَرَّفِ بِلَامِ الحَقِيقَةِ ... إلخ) مثاله : «الرَّجُلُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ المَرْأَةِ». : ومثال العهد: «لَقِيْتُ رَجُلاً فَأَكْرَمْتُ الرَّجُلَ»، واحترز بقوله : حَيْثُ يَكُونُ المَعْهُودُ غَيْرَ مُعَيَّنٍ ممَّا إذا كان المعهود معيَّناً نحو : الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ ﴾ [المائدة: ٣] . (١) في (أ) : «تَعَلُّقِهِ» بدلاً من «تَعَقلِهِ».
Meaning: [the word is placed] for a particularized thing by consideration of its conception (1) not by its specificity, but by a general matter like pointing in the demonstrative noun, and speech or address in the pronoun. This placement is called 'general placement for a specific meaning', contrary to the placement of a proper noun, for it is specific for specific. But exceptions are made from definite nouns for those that are in the strength of an indefinite, like the definite with the lam of reality, or the lam of covenant where the covenanted is unspecified, and the definite by genitive addition (idafa jinsiyya), and the relative pronoun intended for the genus, for they are certainly universals; see the Epistle of al-Aḍud. (3) The third: the particular in the previous sense is called 'the real particular' because its particularity is with respect to its essence. Qisara. His statement: 'by consideration of his conception' means that the assigner considers a common matter among particularized particulars, like speech, and says, for example: This word is placed for each one of these particularized particulars in its specificity such that nothing is understood from it except one in its specificity without the common aspect. He only conceives that common aspect as a tool for the assignment of those particulars, not because it is the assigned meaning. This is the meaning of the placement being general and the assigned meaning being specific. Al-Sayyid said in the glosses on Sharh al-Matali': 'Whoever does not know the general placement for a specific meaning falls into a tight spot (hayṣ bayṣ), i.e., distress and difficulty.' His statement: 'Contrary to the placement of a proper noun' — this is the second of the three divisions into which al-Aḍud divided the subject-word in his epistle. The first is general placement for a specific meaning, which preceded. The third is the placement of the word 'rajul' for its meaning, i.e., what was placed for a general matter in a general placement. As for the converse of the first, which is specific placement for a general meaning, it is impossible in existence, because the particular cannot be a tool for observing the universal. His statement: 'But an exception is made' — this exception is included in the third division we mentioned, which is general placement for a general meaning. His statement: 'Like the definite with the lam of reality ... etc.' — its example: 'al-rajulu khairun min al-mar'ati' (The man is better than the woman). And the example of covenant: 'Laqeetu rajulan fa-akramtu al-rajula' (I met a man and honored the man). And he guarded by his statement: 'where the covenanted is unspecified' from the case where the covenanted is specified, like the verse: 'Today I have perfected for you your religion' (al-Ma'ida: 3). (1) In (A): 'ta'alluqihi' instead of 'ta'aqqulihi'.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the concept of 'wad' 'amm li mawdu' lahu khass' (general placement for a specific meaning). It begins by explaining that words like demonstratives ('hadha') and pronouns ('ana', 'anta') are placed for a particularized thing (mushakhkhas) but not by its specific identity; rather, by a general factor like pointing or speech. This type of placement is called general placement for a specific meaning, as opposed to proper nouns (alam) which are specific for specific. The author then lists three types of wad' according to al-Aḍud: (1) general for specific (as just described), (2) specific for specific (proper nouns), and (3) general for general (like the word 'rajul' meaning 'man'). The converse of (1) — specific placement for a general meaning — is impossible because a particular cannot serve as a tool to grasp a universal. Exceptions are discussed: definite nouns that function as indefinites, such as those with lam al-haqiqa (the definite article indicating the essence, e.g., 'al-rajul' in 'Man is better than woman'), lam al-'ahd (the definite article indicating a known but unspecified covenant, e.g., in 'I met a man and honored the man'), idafa jinsiyya (genitive of genus, e.g., 'khātamu dhahabin' meaning 'gold ring'), and relative pronouns intended for the genus (e.g., 'alladhi' referring to a class). These are actually universals and fall under the third type. The author notes a variant reading in manuscript (A): 'ta'alluqihi' instead of 'ta'aqqulihi'. The margin note 'Qisara' appears again.

Key Terms
وضع عام لموضوع له خاص
علم
وضع خاص لخاص
وضع عام لعام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following words is an example of 'general placement for a specific meaning' (wad' 'amm li mawdu' lahu khass)?
A) The proper noun 'Muhammad'
B) The word 'rajul' meaning 'man'
C) The pronoun 'anta' (you)
D) The definite article in 'al-rajulu' when referring to a known person

Key Takeaway
Words are placed in one of three ways; the fourth way (specific-for-general) is logically impossible because a particular cannot serve as a tool for a universal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify the following words according to the three types of wad': 'Muhammad' (proper noun), 'rajul' (man), 'anta' (you). For each, explain the tool and the object.
?
Explain in your own words why a word cannot be placed specifically for a general meaning. Use the commentator's reasoning about the particular not being a tool for the universal.

When Definite Nouns Act as Universals
Author discusses exceptions to definite nouns that are universals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which definite nouns (ma'arif) are actually universal in meaning, and distinguish them from truly specific definite nouns.

Core Idea
Not every definite noun is specific; some, like those with lam al-haqiqa, refer to the essence and are universal.

The commentator notes an important exception: some definite nouns function like universals. This often occurs with the definite article indicating the essence (lam al-haqiqa), an unspecified covenant (lam al-'ahd), genitive of genus (idafa jinsiyya), and relative pronouns for genus. These are actually universals and fall under the third type of wad'.

Guided Path
1
List the four exceptional definite nouns
From the passage, identify: (1) definite with lam al-haqiqa, (2) definite with lam al-'ahd where the covenanted is unspecified, (3) definite by idafa jinsiyya, (4) relative pronoun intended for the genus. Write them down.
The passage states they are 'certainly universals'.
2
Understand lam al-haqiqa
Lam al-haqiqa indicates the essence or reality of a thing, not a specific instance. The example given is 'al-rajulu khairun min al-mar'ati' (Man is better than woman). Here 'al-rajulu' refers to the genus 'man', not a particular man.
Contrast with lam al-'ahd which refers to a known but unspecified individual.
3
Apply to examples
Practice identifying whether the definite noun in a Quranic verse or fiqh text is universal or specific. For instance, 'al-yawma akmaltu lakum dinakum' – is the 'al-yawm' specific or universal? The commentator notes it is a specific day (covenant specified), so not universal.
4
Explain why these are universals
Each of these types refers to a genus or kind, not a particular. They are 'in the strength of an indefinite' because they can be paraphrased with a universal quantifier. For example, 'al-rajulu' in 'al-rajulu khairun' means 'every man' or 'mankind in general'.
This places them under the third type of wad': general-for-general.

Three Types of Wad' and the Concept of General-for-Specific Posting
Commentator defines three types of wad' and illustrates with examples from Ism al-Ishara and Dhamir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of wad' and explain the logical mechanism of wad' 'amm li-mawdu' lahu khass using examples from ism al-ishara and dhamir.

Core Idea
General posting for a specific referent uses a universal attribute as a tool to pin down a particular.

This passage from the commentary on al-Sullam clarifies a subtle but essential type of linguistic posting: a word can be assigned to a specific referent by way of a universal attribute. This concept, known as wad' 'amm li-mawdu' lahu khass, is the key to understanding how pointer nouns and pronouns function as definite yet conceptually mediated items in Arabic. Without grasping this, one may confuse the scope of many terms in usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of wad'
From the passage, note the three divisions: general-for-specific (wad' 'amm li-mawdu' lahu khass), specific-for-specific (wad' khass li-khass), and general-for-general (wad' 'amm li-'amm).
The third type is exemplified by the word 'man' for the universal concept of man.
2
Analyze the general-for-specific type
Focus on the definition: the word is assigned to a specific referent by considering a universal attribute. The examples are ism al-ishara (pointer noun) and dhamir (pronoun). For 'hadha', the universal attribute is pointing; for 'ana' (I), it is speaking; for 'anta' (you), it is addressing.
The universal attribute is the tool, not the referent.
3
Contrast with specific-for-specific and general-for-general
Specific-for-specific (proper nouns like 'Zaid') directly refers to an individual without a universal intermediary. General-for-general (like 'man') refers to a universal concept. Understand why specific-for-general is impossible: a particular cannot serve as a tool to grasp a universal.
4
Connect to the quote from al-Sayyid
Al-Sayyid al-Sharif warns that ignorance of this concept leads to 'hayb wa-sayb' (narrowness). Reflect on why this concept is crucial for distinguishing the scope of terms.

أَيْ : لِمُشَخَصَ بِاعْتِبَارِ تَعَقْلِهِ (۱) لَا بِخُصُوصِهِ، بَلْ بِأَمْرٍ عَامٌ كَالإِشَارَةِ فِي اسْمِ الإِشَارَةِ، وَالتَّكَلُّمِ أَوِ الخِطَابِ فِي الضَّمِيرِ، وَيُسَمَّى هَذَا الوَضْعُ: «وَضْعاً عَامَّا لِمَوْضُوعِ لَهُ خَاصٌ»، بِخِلَافِ وَضْعِ العَلَمِ، فَإِنَّهُ خَاصٌ لِخَاصٌ لَكِنْ يُسْتَثْنَى مِنَ المَعَارِفِ مَا كَانَ مِنْهَا فِي قُوَّةِ النَّكِرَةِ كَـ : المُعَرَّفِ بِلَامِ الحَقِيقَةِ، أَوِ العَهْدِ حَيْثُ يَكُونُ المَعْهُودُ غَيْرَ مُعَيَّنِ، وَالمُعَرَّفِ بالإِضَافَةِ الجِنْسِيَّةِ، وَالمَوْصُولِ الَّذِي يُرَادُ بِهِ الجِنْسُ ، فَإِنَّهَا كُلِّيَّاتٌ قَطعاً ؛ انْظُرْ رِسَالَةِ العَضُدِ». (۳) - الثَّالِثُ : الجُزْنِيُّ بِالمَعْنَى السَّابِقِ يُسَمَّى : «الجُزْئِيَّ الحَقِيقِيَّ»؛ لِأَنَّ جُزْئِيَّتَهُ بِالنَّظَرِ إِلَى ذَاتِهِ . قصارة. قوله : (بِاعْتِبَارِ تَعَقلِهِ) معناه : أنَّ الواضع يعتبر أمراً مشتركاً بين جزئيات مشخصات ك: التكلم، ويقول مثلاً : هذا اللفظ موضوع لكلِّ واحدٍ من هذه الجزئيات المشخّصات بخصوصه بحيث لا يفهم منه إلَّا واحدٌ بخصوصه دون القدر المشترك، وإنما يتعقل ذلك القدر المشترك ليكون آلة للوضع لتلك الجزئيات، لا لأنَّه هو الموضوع له، هذا معنى كون الوضع عاما والموضوع له خاصا قال السَّيِّد في حواشي شرح المطالع : ومن لم يعرف الوضع العام لموضوع له خاص وقع في حيص بيص؛ أي: ضيق وشدة. قوله : (بِخِلَافِ وَضْعِ العَلَمِ) هذا هو القسم الثاني مِنَ الأقسام الثَّلاثة التي قسم العضدُ في رسالته اللفظ الموضوع إليها ؛ والأوَّل: وضع عام لموضوع له خاص وهو الذي تقدم، والثالث : وضع لفظة رجل لمعناه؛ أي: ما وضع لأمر عام وضعاً عاماً ، وأمَّا عكس الأول وهو وضع خاص لعام فمحال الوجود؛ إذ لا يكون الجزئي آلة لملاحظة الكلّيّ . قوله : (لَكِنْ يُسْتَثْنَى) هذا المستثنى هو داخل في القسم الثَّالث الذي ذكرناه، وهو وضع عام لموضوع له عام. :قوله :(كَـ : المُعَرَّفِ بِلَامِ الحَقِيقَةِ ... إلخ) مثاله : «الرَّجُلُ خَيْرٌ مِنَ المَرْأَةِ». : ومثال العهد: «لَقِيْتُ رَجُلاً فَأَكْرَمْتُ الرَّجُلَ»، واحترز بقوله : حَيْثُ يَكُونُ المَعْهُودُ غَيْرَ مُعَيَّنٍ ممَّا إذا كان المعهود معيَّناً نحو : الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ ﴾ [المائدة: ٣] . (1) في (أ) : «تَعَلُّقِهِ» بدلاً من «تَعَقلِهِ».
Meaning: for a specific individual by considering its universal (1) not by its particularity, but by a general matter like the pointer in the pointer noun, and the speaking or the addressing in the pronoun. This posting is called 'general posting for a specific referent', unlike the posting of a proper noun, for it is specific for a specific. However, exception is made from the definite nouns those that are in the strength of indefinite, such as: the definite with the article of reality, or the definite with the article of familiar where the familiar is unspecified, and the definite by genitive construction of genus, and the relative pronoun intended for the genus, for they are surely universals; look at al-‘Aḍud’s treatise. (3) The third: the particular in the previous sense is called 'the real particular', because its particularity is with respect to its essence. Short. His saying: (by considering its universal) means: the positer considers a matter common among individual specific things like speaking, and says for example: this utterance is posted for each one of these particular specific things specifically, so that nothing is understood from it except one specifically without the common element; rather, he mentally grasps that common element to be a tool for posting for those particulars, not because it is the referent. This is the meaning of the posting being general and the referent specific. Al-Sayyid said in his marginalia on Sharh al-Mutali': 'Whoever does not know the general posting for a specific referent falls into a tight spot; i.e., narrowness and difficulty.' His saying: (unlike the posting of a proper noun) this is the second division of the three divisions into which al-‘Aḍud divided the posted word in his treatise; the first is general posting for a specific referent, which is what preceded; the third is posting the word 'man' for its meaning; i.e., what is posted for a general matter in a general way. As for the opposite of the first, namely specific posting for a general one, it is impossible of existence, because the particular cannot be a tool for noticing the universal. His saying: (but exception is made) this excepted category falls under the third division we mentioned, and it is general posting for a general referent. His saying: (like the definite with the article of reality... etc.) example: 'The man is better than woman'. Example of the definite with familiar: 'I met a man and honored the man'. He guarded by his saying: 'where the familiar is unspecified' from when the familiar is specified, like: 'Today I have perfected your religion for you' (Q. 5:3). (1) In (A): 'by considering its attachment' instead of 'by considering its universal'.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Sullam al-Murunayni explains the concept of al-wad' al-'amm li-mawdu' lahu khass (general posting for a specific referent). The commentator begins by defining it: a word is posted for a specific individual not by its particularity but by considering a universal attribute, such as the pointer in pointer nouns (e.g., 'this') or the speaker/address in pronouns. This type is called 'general posting for a specific referent'. It is contrasted with the posting of proper nouns (alam), which is specific for a specific. However, an exception is made: some definite nouns function like universals because they are not truly definite. Examples include: nouns defined by lam al-haqiqa (like 'the man' meaning 'man as a species'), nouns with lam al-'ahd where the familiar is unspecified, genitive constructions of genus, and relative pronouns intended for the genus. These are all universals. The commentator then cites al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani: misunderstanding this kind of posting leads to confusion. Next, he explains the three divisions from al-‘Aḍud’s treatise: (i) general posting for a specific referent (the one just described), (ii) specific posting for a specific referent (proper nouns), and (iii) general posting for a general referent (e.g., the word 'man' for the concept of man). He notes that the opposite of the first—specific posting for a general referent—is impossible because a particular cannot serve as a tool to grasp a universal. The excepted category (the definite nouns that are actually universals) falls under the third division. Examples are provided for lam al-haqiqa, lam al-'ahd, and genitive construction of genus. The passage ends with a textual variant note.

وضع خاص لخاص
وضع عام لعام

Which of the following is an example of wad' 'amm li-mawdu' lahu khass?
A) The proper noun 'Zaid'
B) The pointer noun 'this' (hadha)
C) The general noun 'man' (al-rajul) with lam al-haqiqa
D) The definite noun 'al-rajul' in 'al-rajul khair min al-mar'a'

Key Takeaway
The three types of wad' are essential for determining whether a word refers to a particular or a universal, and the general-for-specific type uses a universal attribute as an intermediary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task: Identify the wad' type for each of the following words: (a) 'Zaid' (proper noun), (b) 'hadha' (this), (c) 'al-rajul' (the man) in a sentence where it refers to the species. Justify each answer by referencing the universal attribute (if any) used in the posting.
?

Exception: Definite Nouns That Are Actually Universals
Commentator defines three types of wad' and illustrates with examples from Ism al-Ishara and Dhamir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which al-ma'arif (definite nouns) are actually universals and classify them under the appropriate type of wad'.

Core Idea
Some definite nouns are universal in scope because they refer to a genus, not a specific individual.

In the same passage, the commentator makes a crucial refinement: not all al-ma'arif are truly definite in reference. Certain types—like those with lam al-haqiqa or unspecified lam al-'ahd—function as universals. This nuance is vital for accurate logical analysis of Arabic texts in tafsir and usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Recall the three types of wad'
Remind yourself of the three divisions: general-for-specific, specific-for-specific, general-for-general. The exception we will examine falls under the third type.
2
Identify the four categories of al-ma'arif that are exceptions
The commentator lists: (1) al-mu'arraf bi-lam al-haqiqa, e.g., 'al-rajul' in 'al-rajul khair min al-mar'a' (indicating the species); (2) al-mu'arraf bi-lam al-'ahd where al-ma'hood is unspecified, e.g., 'al-rajul' after meeting a man; (3) al-mu'arraf bi al-idafa al-jinsiyya (construct genitive of genus); (4) al-mawsul al-murad bihi al-jins (relative pronoun intended for genus).
These are all considered universals (kulliyat) because they do not refer to a specific individual.
3
Understand why they are universals
For lam al-haqiqa, the definiteness indicates the reality of the kind, not a particular. For lam al-'ahd with unspecified familiar, the referent is known but not concretely identified. For idafa jinsiyya, it indicates a type. For mawsul intended for genus, it indicates the whole species.
Thus, these al-ma'arif behave like 'man' in their scope.
4
Classify under the third division
These exceptions confirm that the word is posted for a general referent (the universal concept) and the posting is general. Therefore, they are instances of wad' 'amm li-'amm.

The Relative Particular and Its Distinction from the Real Particular
Commentator defines al-juz'i al-idafi and distinguishes it from al-haqiqi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the real particular (al-juz'i al-haqiqi) and the relative particular (al-juz'i al-idafi) by applying the criterion of whether the conception prevents sharing.

Core Idea
A relative particular is any meaning falling under a universal; a real particular must also prevent sharing.

In this passage from the commentary on al-Sullam al-Murunayni, the commentator clarifies two types of 'particular' in logic. The distinction hinges on whether the conception of the term itself prevents it from applying to more than one thing. Understanding this difference is essential for precise definition and reasoning in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of particular
Locate the terms 'al-juz'i al-haqiqi' and 'al-juz'i al-idafi' in the Arabic. Note that the commentator defines al-idafi first.
The real particular is also called 'haqiqi', the relative 'idafi'.
2
Understand the defining criterion
For al-idafi, the only condition is that the meaning falls under a universal. For al-haqiqi, the conception of the term itself must prevent sharing (e.g., 'Zaid' cannot apply to another).
Examples in the text: 'Zaid' (haqiqi and idafi), 'man' (idafi only), 'human' (idafi only).
3
Analyze the relationship of generality
The commentator states that al-idafi is 'absolutely more general' than al-haqiqi. Verify that every real particular is also relative, but not conversely. Test with examples.
This is because al-idafi includes terms whose conception does not prevent sharing.
4
Apply to the subdivision of al-haqiqi
The real particular divides into proper noun of a person ('alam shakhs) and proper noun of a genus ('alam jins). Both prevent sharing within their scope.
'Alam shakhs: Zaid. 'Alam jins: 'human' used as a proper name for the species.

فصل في مباحث الألفاظ وَيُطْلَقُ الجُزْنِيُّ أَيْضاً عِنْدَهُمْ عَلَى كُلِّ مَعْنِّى مُنْدَرج تَحْتَ كُلِّيِّ، وَيُسَمُّونَهُ: «الجُزْئِيَّ الإِضَافِيَّ»؛ سَوَاءٌ مَنَعَ تَصَوُّرُهُ الشَّرِكَةَ فِيهِ كَـ: «زَيْدِ ، فَهُوَ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ كُلّي، بَلْ كُلِّيَّات : الإِنْسَانِ»، وَ : «الحَيَوَانِ»، أَوْ لَمْ يَمْنَعْهَا كَـ : الرَّجُلِ ، فَهُوَ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الإِنْسَانِ مَثَلاً، وَكَ: «الإِنْسَانِ فَإِنَّهُ مُنْدَرجُ تَحْتَ الحَيَوَانِ»، ... وَهَكَذَا . وَبِهِ تَعْلَمُ : أَنَّ الإِضَافِيَّ أَعَمُّ بِإِطْلَاقِ مِنَ الحَقِيقِيّ، وَسُمِّيَ: «إِضَافِيَّا»؛ لِأَنَّ جُزْنِيَّتَهُ بِالإِضَافَةِ لِمَا انْدَرَجَ هُوَ فِيهِ. كَـ (٤) - الرَّابِعُ : الجُزْنِيُّ الحَقِيقِيُّ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : عَلَمٍ شَخْصٍ، وَإِلَى عَلَمٍ جِنْسِ . قصارة. ومثال المعرَّف بالإضافة الجنسيَّة : جَاءَ غُلَامُ الأَمِيرِ» حيث لا عهد، وهو مبني على ما حققه السَّيِّد من مجيء تعريف الإضافة جنسيا، واحترز بـ «الإضافة الجنسيَّة مِنَ العهد؛ نحو: «جَاءَ غُلَامُكَ إذا كان الغلام معهوداً بينكما. ومثال الموصول الَّذي يُراد به الجنس: قوله تعالى: ﴿كَمَثَلِ الَّذِي يَنْعِيُّ) [البقرة: ١٧١] أي: يصيح واحترز بالقيد عن نحو: إِنَّ الَّذِي فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْءَانَ ﴾ [القصص : ٨٥] . ومِنَ الكلّيّ أيضاً : ضمير الغيبة العائد على كلّي على ما ارتضاه بعض المحققين. قوله : عَلَى كُلِّ مَعْنِّى مُنْدَرِجِ تَحْتَ كُلّي) معنى اندراجه تحته : دخول جميع ما يصدق عليه ( تحت الكلّيّ، وذلك خاص بالأخص مطلقاً كـ «الإنسان المندرج جميع مصدوقاته تحت «الحيوان»، بخلاف الأخص من وجه كـ الأبيض والإنسان، فليس أحدهما جزئيا بالإضافة إلى الآخر، وإن كان كل منهما داخلاً تحت الآخر ببعض أفراده ؛ قاله السعد، خلافاً للكاتبي . ثمَّ إِنَّ في قول الشَّارح : على كلِّ معنى) بحثاً؛ حيث ذكر لفظة «كل» مع أنَّ التَّعريف للماهية، و«كل» للأفراد. وأجيب بأنَّ المعرَّف هو ما بعد «كل»، وفائدة الإتيان بها التَّصريح بأنَّ الحد مطرد منعكس من أول الأمر. عن قوله : ( وَبِهِ تَعْلَمُ : أَنَّ الإِضَافِيَّ أَعَمُّ بِإِطْلَاقٍ أي : لأنَّ كلَّ جزئي حقيقي فهو جزئي إضافي، ولا عكس : أمَّا الأوَّل : فلاندراج كل شخص تحت ماهيَّته المعرَّاة عن المشخصات، كما إذا جردنا زيداً المشخّصات التي صار بها شخصاً معيناً بقيت الماهية الإنسانية وهي أعم.
Section on Topics of Utterances. 'The particular' is also used by them for every meaning that falls under a universal, and they call it 'the relative particular'; whether its conception prevents sharing in it, like 'Zaid', for he falls under a universal, nay universals: 'human' and 'animal', or does not prevent it, like 'man', for he falls under 'human' for instance, and like 'human', for it falls under 'animal', and so on. By this you know that the relative is absolutely more general than the real, and it is called 'relative' because its particularity is relative to what it falls under. Like (4) The fourth: the real particular divides into: a proper noun of a person and a proper noun of a genus. Short. Example of the definite by genitive construction of genus: 'The servant of the prince came' where there is no familiar, and it is based on what al-Sayyid verified about the definite by genitive construction being generic; and he guarded by 'genitive construction of genus' from the familiar, like: 'Your servant came' if the servant is familiar between you. Example of the relative pronoun intended for the genus: Allah's saying: 'Like the one who shouts' (Q. 2:171) i.e., shouts; and he guarded by the restriction from like: 'Indeed, the One who imposed the Qur'an upon you' (Q. 28:85). And from the universal also: the pronoun of absence returning to a universal according to what some investigators approved. His saying: 'for every meaning falling under a universal' means: its falling under it: the inclusion of all that it applies to under the universal, and that is specific to the absolute more specific like 'human' all of whose instances fall under 'animal', unlike the more specific in some aspects like 'white' and 'human', for neither is particular relative to the other, even though each of them falls under the other in some of its individuals; this was said by al-Sa'd, contrary to al-Katibi. Then, in the commentator's saying 'for every meaning' there is a discussion, since he mentioned the word 'every' while the definition is for the essence, and 'every' is for individuals. It was answered that the defined is what is after 'every', and the benefit of bringing it is to declare that the definition is coextensive and counterextensive from the first. From his saying: (By this you know that the relative is absolutely more general) i.e., because every real particular is a relative particular, and not conversely. As for the first: because every person falls under his stripped essence of particularities, as when we strip Zaid of the particularities by which he became a specific person, the human essence remains, and it is more general.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Sullam al-Murunayni discusses the two types of 'particular' (juz'i) in logic: the real particular (al-juz'i al-haqiqi) and the relative particular (al-juz'i al-idafi). The commentator begins by defining the relative particular: any meaning that falls under a universal, whether it prevents participation (like the proper noun 'Zaid', which falls under 'human' and 'animal') or not (like 'man', which falls under 'human'). The term 'relative' is used because its particularity is relative to the universal under which it falls. The commentator then states that the relative particular is absolutely more general than the real particular, because every real particular is also a relative particular, but not conversely. Next, the fourth point: the real particular divides into two: a proper noun of a person ('alam shakhs, e.g., Zaid) and a proper noun of a genus ('alam jins, e.g., 'human' used as a proper noun for the concept). Examples are given for the definite by genitive construction of genus and relative pronoun intended for genus, with Qur'anic verses. The commentator also discusses a point of contention: the phrase 'for every meaning' (kull ma'na) in the definition uses the word 'every', which normally refers to individuals, but the definition is for the essence. The answer is that the definition is for what follows 'every', and 'every' is used to indicate that the definition is coextensive from the beginning. Finally, the commentator explains why the relative is more general: stripping a person of its particularities leaves a more general essence.

الجزيئي الإضافي
الاندراج
علم شخص
علم جنس

Key Takeaway
The relative particular is more general than the real particular, and the distinction hinges on whether the conception of the term prevents sharing.

The Relational Particular: Definition and Analysis
Definition and expansion of the relational particular

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the relational particular, distinguish it from the real particular, and explain why the word 'every' is used in its definition.

Core Idea
Every meaning under a universal is a relational particular, including proper and common nouns.

This lesson unpacks the definition of the relational particular as given by Islamic logicians. The author not only defines the term but also provides examples and addresses a subtle question about the wording of the definition. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper logical classification in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the sentence where the author states: 'ويطلق الجزئي أيضا عندهم على كل معنى مندرج تحت كلي'. This is the core definition.
2
Examine the two examples
The author gives Zayd (real particular) and rajul (common noun) as both falling under universals. Note that Zayd prevents sharing while rajul does not, yet both are relational particulars.
This shows the relational particular includes both types.
3
Understand the generality claim
The passage proves that every real particular is a relational particular, but not vice versa. Why? Because stripping individuators reveals a universal essence.
Example: stripping Zayd of his individuators leaves 'human', which is a universal and thus a relational particular as well.
4
Resolve the 'كل' objection
The commentator uses 'كل' (every) in the definition. Why? The answer: it is to emphasize that the definition is coextensive and co-exclusive from the start.
The term 'كل' is not part of the definiens but a rhetorical device for clarity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُطْلَقُ الْجُزْئِيُّ أَيْضاً عِنْدَهُمْ عَلَى كُلِّ مَعْنَىً مُنْدَرِجٍ تَحْتَ كُلِّيٍّ، وَيُسَمُّونَهُ: «الْجُزْئِيَّ الْإِضَافِيَّ»؛ سَوَاءٌ مَنَعَ تَصَوُّرُهُ الشَّرِكَةَ فِيهِ كَـ: «زَيْدٍ» فَهُوَ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ كُلِّيٍّ، بَلْ كُلِّيَّاتٍ: «الْإِنْسَانِ»، وَ: «الْحَيَوَانِ»، أَوْ لَمْ يَمْنَعْهَا كَـ: «الرَّجُلِ»، فَهُوَ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الْإِنْسَانِ مَثَلاً، وَكَـ: «الْإِنْسَانِ» فَإِنَّهُ مُنْدَرِجٌ تَحْتَ الْحَيَوَانِ، وَهَكَذَا. وَبِهِ تَعْلَمُ: أَنَّ الْإِضَافِيَّ أَعَمُّ بِإِطْلَاقٍ مِنَ الْحَقِيقِيِّ، وَسُمِّيَ: «إِضَافِيَّاً»؛ لِأَنَّ جُزْئِيَّتَهُ بِالْإِضَافَةِ لِمَا انْدَرَجَ هُوَ فِيهِ. ثُمَّ إِنَّ فِي قَوْلِ الشَّارِحِ: «عَلَى كُلِّ مَعْنَىً» بَحْثاً؛ حَيْثُ ذَكَرَ لَفْظَةَ «كُلِّ» مَعَ أَنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ لِلْمَاهِيَّةِ، وَ«كُلُّ» لِلْأَفْرَادِ. وَأُجِيبَ بِأَنَّ الْمُعَرَّفَ هُوَ مَا بَعْدَ «كُلِّ»، وَفَائِدَةُ الْإِتْيَانِ بِهَا التَّصْرِيحُ بِأَنَّ الْحَدَّ مُطَّرِدٌ مُنْعَكِسٌ مِنْ أَوَّلِ الْأَمْرِ. قَوْلُهُ: (وَبِهِ تَعْلَمُ: أَنَّ الْإِضَافِيَّ أَعَمُّ بِإِطْلَاقٍ) أَيْ: لِأَنَّ كُلَّ جُزْئِيٍّ حَقِيقِيٍّ فَهُوَ جُزْئِيٌّ إِضَافِيٌّ، وَلَا عَكْسَ: أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ: فَلِانْدِرَاجِ كُلِّ شَخْصٍ تَحْتَ مَاهِيَّتِهِ الْمُعَرَّاةِ عَنِ الْمُشَخِّصَاتِ، كَمَا إِذَا جَرَّدْنَا زَيْداً عَنِ الْمُشَخِّصَاتِ الَّتِي صَارَ بِهَا شَخْصاً مُعَيَّناً بَقِيَتِ الْمَاهِيَّةُ الْإِنْسَانِيَّةُ وَهِيَ أَعَمُّ. وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي: فَلِجَوَازِ كَوْنِ الْجُزْئِيِّ الْإِضَافِيِّ كُلِّيَّاً، وَامْتِنَاعِ كَوْنِ الْجُزْئِيِّ الْحَقِيقِيِّ كَذَلِكَ.
And the particular is also used by them for every meaning that falls under a universal, and they call it 'the relational particular'; whether its conception prevents sharing in it like 'Zayd' – for it falls under a universal, nay universals: 'human' and 'animal' – or it does not prevent it like 'man' – for it falls under 'human' for example, and like 'human' for it falls under 'animal', and so on. And by it you know that the relational is absolutely more general than the real, and it is called 'relational' because its particularity is by relation to what it falls under. Then there is a discussion in the commentator's statement: 'for every meaning' – since he mentioned the word 'every' while the definition is for the essence, and 'every' is for individuals. And it was answered that the defined is what is after 'every', and the benefit of bringing it is to explicitly state that the definition is coextensive and co-exclusive from the very beginning. His statement: (And by it you know that the relational is absolutely more general) meaning: because every real particular is a relational particular, and not vice versa: as for the first, because every person falls under his essence stripped of individuators, just as if we strip Zayd of the individuators by which he became a specific person, the human essence remains and it is more general. And as for the second, because it is possible for the relational particular to be universal, and it is impossible for the real particular to be so.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'relational particular' (الجزئي الإضافي) as used by logicians. It begins by stating that the term 'particular' is applied to any meaning that falls under a universal. This is the relational particular, so called because its particularity is relative to what it falls under. The passage then distinguishes two cases: the particular may prevent sharing in its conception, like the proper name 'Zayd' (which is unique to one person and falls under universals like 'human' and 'animal'), or it may not prevent sharing, like the common noun 'man' (which falls under 'human' as its species, and 'human' falls under 'animal'). The author then notes that the relational particular is more general (أعم بإطلاق) than the real particular, meaning every real particular is relational but not vice versa. The proof: any real particular (a specific individual) when stripped of its individuators leaves an essence that is more general and falls under a higher universal. Conversely, a relational particular like 'man' can be a universal itself. The passage also addresses a subtle point about the commentator's use of the word 'every' (كل) in the definition: although definitions are of essences, 'every' is used to emphasize that the definition is coextensive and co-exclusive from the outset. This guards against a misunderstanding that the definition might not cover all cases.

الجُزْئِيُّ الحَقِيقِيُّ

Division of Real Particular into Proper Nouns of Person and Genus
Matn states the division; commentary defines each type with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a proper noun of person from a proper noun of genus by identifying whether its referent is determined externally or in the mind.

Core Idea
Real particulars name either external individuals or mental genera.

This lesson unpacks a key division in the theory of universals: the real particular splits into two types of proper nouns. Understanding this distinction helps you grasp how terms can name either concrete individuals or mental species, a crucial point for definition and analogy in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the division
Read the matn statement: the real particular divides into two types. Find those two categories in the Arabic.
2
Define the first type
The first is 'alam shakhsi: its referent is determined in external reality, outside the mind. Examples: Zayd, Mecca.
3
Define the second type
The second is 'alam jinsi: its referent is determined in the mind as a conceptual species. Examples: Usama and Abu al-Harith for lion.
4
Contrast the two types
Notice that 'alam shakhsi points to an individual in the world, while 'alam jinsi points to a mental concept representing a whole genus.
5
Test with examples
Given a proper noun, decide whether it refers to an external individual (person) or a mental genus. Use the definitions as criteria.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرَّابِعُ: الْجُزْئِيُّ الْحَقِيقِيُّ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى: عَلَمٍ شَخْصِيٍّ، وَإِلَى عَلَمٍ جِنْسِيٍّ. فَالْأَوَّلُ: «مَا تَعَيَّنَ مُسَمَّاهُ فِي الْخَارِجِ عَنِ الذَّهْنِ»؛ كَـ: زَيْدٍ، وَمَكَّةَ. وَالثَّانِي: «مَا تَعَيَّنَ مُسَمَّاهُ فِي الذِّهْنِ»؛ كَـ: أُسَامَةَ، وَأَبِي الْحَارِثِ لِلْأَسَدِ.
The fourth: the real particular divides into a proper noun of person and a proper noun of genus. The first is: 'that whose named entity is determined in the external [reality] outside the mind'; like 'Zayd' and 'Mecca'. And the second: 'that whose named entity is determined in the mind'; like 'Usama' and 'Abu al-Harith' for the lion.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage presents a classification of the real particular (الجزئي الحقيقي). The matn states that the real particular is divided into two types: a proper noun of a person (علم شخصي) and a proper noun of a genus (علم جنسي). The commentary expands on each. The first type (proper noun of a person) is defined as that whose referent is determined in the external world, outside the mind. Examples include 'Zayd' (a specific person) and 'Mecca' (a specific city). The second type (proper noun of a genus) is defined as that whose referent is determined in the mind. Examples include 'Usama' (a proper name for a lion) and 'Abu al-Harith' (a nickname for a lion). The key distinction is that proper nouns of persons refer to individuals in external reality, while proper nouns of genera refer to an essence that is mentally present as a specific concept, not tied to external individuals.

Key Terms
عَلَمٌ شَخْصِيٌّ
عَلَمٌ جِنْسِيٌّ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Cairo
B) Ahmad
C) Usama (for lion)
D) Book

Key Takeaway
The real particular divides into two types of proper nouns based on whether their referent is determined externally (person) or mentally (genus).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Distinguishing Proper Noun of Genus from Common Noun of Genus
Author presents the dispute and Ibn Khatimah's resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the proper noun of genus (علم الجنس) and the common noun of genus (اسم الجنس) based on the criterion of mental presence (العهدية) and identify the metaphorical use of the proper noun for external individuals.

Core Idea
The proper noun of genus names the essence as mentally present; its use for an external individual is always metaphorical.

In this passage, the author clarifies a debated distinction between two types of nouns used for genera: the proper noun of genus (علم الجنس) and the common noun of genus (اسم الجنس). While both denote the essence, the key difference lies in the connotation of mental presence (عهدية) in the proper noun. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct interpretation of terms in logical definitions and in Arabic grammar, especially when applied to Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Find علم الجنس (like 'Usama' for lion) and اسم الجنس (like 'asad' for lion) in the Arabic. Note that both denote the genus essence but differ in the connotation of mental presence.
2
Understand the definition of علم الجنس
According to Ibn Khatimah, it is placed for the essence to distinguish it from other mental essences, disregarding external individuals. It indicates the essence as well-known (عهدية) in the mind.
This mental presence is what makes it a 'proper' noun of the genus.
3
Contrast with اسم الجنس
The common noun of genus denotes the mental essence without the connotation of well-knownness or mental presence. It is a general term for the genus.
اسم الجنس lacks the element of 'عهدية'.
4
Apply the distinction to usage for external individuals
When علم الجنس is used for a specific external individual (e.g., 'Usama' for a lion), it is metaphorical, not literal, because the literal meaning includes the mental presence, which the individual does not possess.
The individual only corresponds to the essence in itself, not the mental presence.
5
Recognize the scholarly disagreement
Some scholars (al-Sa'd, al-Mahalli) considered it literal, but the chosen view (Ibn al-Hajib, al-Radi) says it is metaphorical. Understand the reasoning: individuals entail the essence in itself, not the mental presence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَدِ اضْطَرَبُوا فِي الْفَرْقِ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ اسْمِ الْجِنْسِ كَـ: «أَسَدِ»، وَالْمُخْتَارُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مَا حَقَّقَهُ ابْنُ خَاتِمَةَ: أَنَّ عَلَمَ الْجِنْسِ مَوْضُوعٌ لِلْحَقِيقَةِ؛ لِيُمَيِّزَهَا عَنْ غَيْرِهَا مِنَ الْحَقَائِقِ الذِّهْنِيَّةِ مَعَ قَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنْ وُجُودِهَا فِي أَفْرَادِهَا الْخَارِجِيَّةِ، وَاسْمُ الْجِنْسِ مَوْضُوعٌ لِلْحَقِيقَةِ الذِّهْنِيَّةِ. وَهَذَا الْفَرْقُ الْمُخْتَارُ عِنْدَ الشَّارِحِ هُوَ مَا حَقَّقَهُ أَيْضاً الْعَضُدُ وَالسَّيِّدُ الشَّرِيفُ وَالدَّمَامِينِيُّ. قَوْلُهُ: (مَعَ قَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنْ وُجُودِهَا فِي أَفْرَادِهَا ... إلخ) مَعْنَاهُ: أَنَّ عَلَمَ الْجِنْسِ عِنْدَهُمْ مَوْضُوعٌ لِلْحَقِيقَةِ الْمُتَّحِدَةِ فِي الذِّهْنِ الْمُشَخَّصَةِ فِيهِ الَّتِي لَمْ تُلاحَظْ فِيهَا الْأَفْرَادُ الْبَتَّةَ، دَالٍّ عَلَى عَهْدِيَّتِهَا فِي ذِهْنِ الْمُخَاطِبِ بِجَوْهَرِ لَفْظِهِ، وَحِينَئِذٍ فَاسْتِعْمَالُهُ فِي فَرْدٍ خَارِجِيٍّ مُبْهَمٍ أَوْ مُعَيَّنٍ؛ نَحْوَ: «إِنْ لَقِيتَ أُسَامَةَ فَفِرَّ مِنْهُ، وَهَذَا أُسَامَةُ مُقْبِلاً» إِنَّمَا هُوَ مِنْ حَيْثُ مُطَابَقَةُ الْفَرْدِ لِلْحَقِيقَةِ أَيْ: صِدْقُهَا عَلَيْهِ مِنْ حَيْثُ هِيَ هِيَ، لَا مِنْ حَيْثُ عَهْدِيَّتِهَا فِي ذِهْنِ الْمُخَاطَبِ الْمُعْتَبَرَةِ فِي عَلَمِ الْجِنْسِ، فَاسْتِعْمَالُهُ فِي الْفَرْدِ مُطْلَقاً مَجَازٌ عَلَى مَا صَرَّحَ بِهِ ابْنُ الْحَاجِبِ وَالرَّضِيُّ وَتَبِعَهُمَا شَيْخُنَا سَيِّدِي الطَّيِّبُ فِي حَوَاشِيهِ عَلَى ضِجٍّ، لَا حَقِيقَةٌ كَمَا تَوَهَّمَهُ السَّعْدُ وَتَبِعَهُ الْمَحَلِّيُّ وَغَيْرُهُ؛ لِأَنَّ الْأَفْرَادَ مُسْتَلْزِمَةٌ لِلْحَقِيقَةِ مِنْ حَيْثُ هِيَ هِيَ، لَا مِنْ حَيْثُ الْحُضُورِ الَّذِي هُوَ مَعْنَى التَّعْرِيفِ.
And they have disagreed about the difference between it and the common noun of genus like 'asad' (lion). The chosen view from that is what Ibn Khatimah verified: that the proper noun of genus is placed for the essence to distinguish it from other mental essences, disregarding its existence in its external individuals, and the common noun of genus is placed for the mental essence. And this chosen distinction according to the commentator is also what was verified by al-‘Adud, al-Sayyid al-Sharif, and al-Damamini. His statement: 'with disregard of its existence in its individuals... etc.' meaning: that the proper noun of genus according to them is placed for the single essence in the mind, determined in it, in which individuals are not considered at all, indicating its being well-known in the mind of the addressee by the substance of its word. Then its use for a vague or specific external individual, like: 'If you meet Usama then flee from him, and this is Usama approaching,' is only by virtue of the individual's correspondence to the essence, i.e., its truth applying to it insofar as it is itself, not by virtue of its being well-known in the mind of the addressee which is considered in the proper noun of genus. So its use for an individual absolutely is metaphorical according to what Ibn al-Hajib and al-Radi stated, and our shaykh Sayyidi al-Tayyib followed them in his glosses on [the work] 'Dj', not literal as al-Sa'd imagined and al-Mahalli and others followed him; because individuals entail the essence insofar as it is itself, not insofar as the presence which is the meaning of definition.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage addresses a debated distinction between the proper noun of a genus (علم الجنس) and the common noun of a genus (اسم الجنس). The author reports that scholars disagreed, and the chosen view is that of Ibn Khatimah: the proper noun of genus (like 'Usama' for lion) is placed to denote the essence itself as a mental concept that distinguishes it from other mental concepts, with no consideration of its external individuals. In contrast, the common noun (like 'asad') is placed for the mental essence without that specific determination of mental presence. The passage further explains that when a proper noun of genus is used for a particular external individual (e.g., 'Usama' referring to a specific lion), it is metaphorical (مجاز), not literal, because the literal meaning of the proper noun of genus is tied to the essence as mentally present and well-known (عهدية). The opponents (al-Sa'd, al-Mahalli) thought it was literal, but the author sides with Ibn al-Hajib and al-Radi that it is metaphorical, since the individual only corresponds to the essence in itself, not to the mental presence that is the defining feature of the proper noun of genus.

Key Terms
عَلَمُ الْجِنْسِ (‘alam al-jins): A proper noun that denotes an essence as a mentally present, well-known concept, disregarding external individuals. [Note: This term is contrasted with اسم الجنس; the distinction is standard in Arabic grammar and logic, but the exact definition can vary among scholars.]
اسْمُ الْجِنْسِ (ism al-jins): A common noun that denotes an essence in the mind without the connotation of mental presence or well-knownness. [Note: Stable across the tradition; often used as a general term for genus names.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view in the passage, the proper noun of genus (علم الجنس) is defined as:
A) A noun that denotes the essence as applicable to all individuals
B) A noun that denotes the essence as mentally present and well-known, disregarding individuals
C) A noun that denotes a specific named individual
D) A noun that denotes the essence without any mental consideration

Key Takeaway
The proper noun of genus inherently includes mental presence, making its application to external individuals metaphorical, not literal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. In the following sentence, determine whether the noun 'Usama' is used literally or metaphorically, and justify your answer based on the definition of علم الجنس: 'رأيت أسامة في الغابة' (I saw Usama in the forest).
?
2. Provide a real example from Islamic jurisprudence where distinguishing between علم الجنس and اسم الجنس would affect the application of a legal ruling. Explain your reasoning.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
10 min
Distinction between 'Alam al-Jins and Ism al-Jins
Commentator distinguishes 'alam al-jins from ism al-jins with multiple scholarly views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish 'alam al-jins from ism al-jins based on their definitions and identify the key points of scholarly disagreement.

Core Idea
'Alam al-jins is a mental proper noun; ism al-jins is a generic noun with external reference.

This passage from Bajuri's commentary on al-Sullam al-Munawraq delves into the fine distinction between two types of nouns that express genera: 'alam al-jins (the genus proper noun) and ism al-jins (the genus noun). Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping how definiteness and particularity work in Arabic grammar and logic. We will follow the commentator's analysis and the chosen view of Ibn Khatima.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of 'alam
The commentator first distinguishes 'alam that is particularized in external reality (like Zayd and Mecca) from 'alam that is particularized in the mind (like Usamah and Abu al-Harith for the lion). Note that the second type is what we call 'alam al-jins.
2
Locate Ibn Khatima's definition of 'alam al-jins
Find the sentence where Ibn Khatima's view is presented: 'alam al-jins is posited for the essence to distinguish it from other mental essences while disregarding its existence in external individuals. This is the chosen view for the commentator.
Contrast this with the definition of ism al-jins that follows.
3
Compare the definitions of 'alam al-jins and ism al-jins
According to the first view, ism al-jins is posited for the essence with consideration of its existence in a non-specific external individual (like 'a man'), while 'alam al-jins disregards external individuals entirely. This makes 'alam al-jins particular (juz'ī) and ism al-jins universal (kullī).
The text also gives a second view that ism al-jins is posited for the essence per se, but the first view is the one verified by scholars.
4
Analyze the points of difference between them
On the first view, there are two differences: (1) 'alam al-jins disregards external referents, ism al-jins considers them; (2) 'alam al-jins indicates by its substance that the essence is known (maʿhūdah) to the addressee, while ism al-jins does not. On the second view, the only difference is the additional indication of knownness in 'alam al-jins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَالأَوَّلُ: «مَا تَعَيَّنَ مُسَمَّاهُ فِي الخَارِجِ عَنِ الذَّهْنِ»؛ كَـ: زَيْدٍ، وَمَكَّةَ . وَالثَّانِي: «مَا تَعَيَّنَ مُسَمَّاهُ فِي الذِّهْنِ»؛ كَـ: أَسَامَةَ، وَأَبِي الحَارِثِ لِلأَسَدِ . وَقَدِ اضْطَرَبُوا فِي الفَرْقِ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ اسْمِ الجِنْسِ كَـ: «أَسَدِ»، وَالمُخْتَارُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مَا حَقَّقَهُ ابْنُ خَاتِمَةَ: أَنَّ عَلَمَ الجِنْسِ مَوْضُوعٌ لِلحَقِيقَةِ؛ لِيُمَيِّزَهَا عَنْ غَيْرِهَا مِنَ الحَقَائِقِ الذَّهْنِيَّةِ مَعَ قَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنْ وُجُودِهَا فِي أَفْرَادِهَا الخَارِجِيَّةِ، وَاسْمُ الجِنْسِ مَوْضُوعٌ لِلحَقِيقَةِ الذِّهْنِيَّةِ بِاعْتِبَارِ وُجُودِهَا فِي أَفْرَادِهَا الخَارِجِيَّةِ، وَلِذَا كَانَ الأَوَّلُ جُزْنِيًّا وَالثَّانِي كُلِّيًّا .
ثم قال الشارح: وأَمَّا الثَّاني: فلجواز كون الجزئي الإضافي كلِّيًّا، وامتناع كون الجزئي الحقيقي كذلك. قوله: (مَا تَعَيَّنَ مُسَمَّاهُ فِي الخَارِجِ عَنِ الذَّهْنِ) أي: بلا قيد؛ إذ العَلَم الشَّخصي — كما قال ابن مالك - : اسم يعيّن مسماه تعييناً مطلقاً، ويدخل في هذا القسم العَلَم بالغلبة ك: البيت وابن عمر، فإنَّه علمٌ على شخص معيَّن في الخارج؛ إلَّا أنَّ الوضع فيه بالنَّقل مِنَ المسمى اتفاقي كما صرح به بعض المحققين.
قوله: (فِي الذِّهْنِ) أي: بلا قيد، وهذا محط الفرق بين العَلَم الشَّخصيّ وبين العَلَم الجنسي. قوله: (وَالمُخْتَارُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مَا حَقَّقَهُ ابْنُ خَاتِمَةَ) هو العلامة أبو العباس أحمد بن علي بن خاتمة النَّاظم النَّاثر ذو التأليف الحسنة، توفّي في حدود الثمانين وسبع مئة . وهذا الفرق المختارُ عند الشَّارح هو ما حققه أيضاً العضد والسَّيِّد الشّريف والدماميني .
قوله: (مَعَ قَطْعِ النَّظَرِ عَنْ وُجُودِهَا فِي أَفْرَادِهَا ... إلخ) معناه: أنَّ عَلَم الجنس عندهم موضوع للحقيقة المتحدة في الذهن المشخّصة فيه التي لم تُلاحظ فيها الأفراد البيَّة دال على عهديَّتها في ذهن المخاطب بجوهر لفظه، وحينئذ فاستعماله في فرد خارجي مبهم أو معيَّن؛ نحو: «إن لقيت أسامة ففرّ منه، وهذا أسامة مقبلاً إنَّما هو من حيث مطابقة الفرد الحقيقة أي: صدقها عليه من حيث لا هي هي، من حيث عهديَّتها في ذهن المخاطب المعتبرة في علم الجنس، فاستعماله في الفرد مطلقاً مجاز على ما صرّح به ابن الحاجب والرّضي وتبعهما شيخنا سيدي الطَّيِّب في حواشيه على ضج، لا حقيقة كما توهمه السَّعد وتبعه المحلى وغيره؛ لأنَّ الأفراد مستلزمةٌ للحقيقة من حيث هي هي، لا من حيث الحضور الذي هو معنى التّعريف .
ثم قال في فصل مباحث الألفاظ: بِاعْتِبَارِ وُجُودِهَا فِي أَفْرَادِهَا الخَارِجِيَّةِ، وَلِذَا كَانَ الأَوَّلُ جُزْنِيًّا وَالثَّانِي كُلِّيًّا . قوله: (بِاعْتِبَارِ وُجُودِهَا فِي أَفْرَادِهَا الخَارِجِيَّةِ) أي: فيكون اسم الجنس موضوعاً للماهية وحدة لا بعينها وتسمّى فرداً مبهماً»، و «فرداً منتشراً»، ووحدة شائعة، وهذا القول للآمدي وابن الحاجب والسبكي وسعد الدين. وقيل: إنَّ اسم الجنس موضوع للماهية من حيث هي هي، واستعماله في الفرد إنَّما هو لتحقق الماهية فيه وكونه حاصلاً لها، وهو استعمال حقيقي لا مجازيٌّ؛ لأنَّ اللَّفظ مستعمل في الحقيقة، والفردية مستفادة من خارج، فالفرقُ بين علم الجنس واسمه على القول الأول من وجهين: أحدهما: أنَّ علم الجنس موضوع للماهية مع قطع النظر عن ما صدقاتها، واسم الجنس لها بقيد وجودها في واحدٍ لا بعينه وهو مِنَ الماصدقات . ثانيهما: أنَّ علم الجنس يدلُّ بجوهر لفظه على كون تلك الحقيقة معهودة في ذهن المخاطب حاضرة فيه متصوَّرةً له واسم الجنس لا يدلُّ على عهد أصلاً. وأمَّا على القول الثَّاني فمن وجه واحدٍ وهو: أنَّ كلا منهما وإن كان موضوعاً للماهية مع قطع النظر عن أفرادها، لكن في علم الجنس زيادة قيد، وهو الدَّلالة بجوهر لفظه على كون تلك الحقيقة معهودةً معلومة للمخاطب، واسم الجنس لا يدلُّ على تلك إلَّا بالأداة إن كانت . والخلاف إنَّما هو في موضوع اسم الجنس المنكر، وأمَّا المعرَّف بلام الحقيقة فهو مساو في المعنى لعَلَم الجنس؛ هذا كله حيث قلنا: إنَّ عَلَم الجنس معرفةٌ لفظاً ومعنى، أما إن قلنا: معرفةٌ لفظاً فقط فهو مرادف في المعنى لاسم الجنس كما يقوله ابن مالك والرّضي، فهو حينئذ مِنَ الكليات، وإلى الفرق المذكور بين عَلَم الجنس واسم الجنس أشرت بقولي:
إِذَا أَرَدْتَ الفَرْقَ بَيْنَ عَلَم الجِنْسِ وَاسْمِهِ حَقَّقْ وَافْهَم فَالعَلَمُ الحَقِيقَةُ المُسْتَحْضَرَه فِي الذِّهْنِ وَالْعَ الفَرْدَ أَنْ تَعْتَبِرَه وَالاسْمُ مَا وُضِعَ لِلْحَقِيقَه بِقَيْدِ الإِفْرَادِ فَذِي طَرِيقَه وَقِيلَ: إِنَّ الاِسْمَ لِلْحَقِيقَه مِنْ حَيْثُ مَا هِيَ أَنَّى حَقِيقَه وَالفَرْدُ أَيْضاً فِيهِ غَيْرُ مُعْتَبَر وَأَوَّلُ حَقَّقَهُ ذَوُو النَّظَ
The first: 'what its named is particularized in external [reality] apart from the mind' like Zayd and Mecca. The second: 'what its named is particularized in the mind' like Usamah and Abu al-Harith for the lion. And they have disagreed regarding the distinction between it and the genus noun like 'lion', and the chosen among that is what Ibn Khatima verified: that the genus proper noun is posited for the essence to distinguish it from other mental essences while disregarding its existence in its external individuals, and the genus noun is posited for the mental essence with consideration of its existence in its external individuals, and therefore the first is particular and the second is universal. Then the commentator said: As for the second: because it is possible for the relative particular to be universal, and impossible for the real particular to be so. His saying: (what its named is particularized in external [reality] apart from the mind) i.e. without restriction; for the personal proper noun – as Ibn Malik said – is a noun that specifies its named absolutely, and into this category enters the proper noun by predominance like 'al-Bayt' and 'Ibn 'Umar', for it is a proper noun for a specific person in external reality, except that the coinage in it is by transfer from the named coincidentally as some investigators stated. His saying: (in the mind) i.e. without restriction, and this is the crux of the distinction between the personal proper noun and the genus proper noun. His saying: (and the chosen from that is what Ibn Khatima verified) he is the scholar Abu al-'Abbas Ahmad bin 'Ali bin Khatima, the verse-composer and prose-writer, possessor of good compositions, died around 780. And this chosen distinction according to the commentator is also what 'Adud, al-Sayyid al-Sharif and al-Damamini verified. His saying: (with disregard of its existence in its individuals... etc.) its meaning: that the genus proper noun in their view is posited for the essence unified in the mind, specified there, in which no individuals are considered, indicating its givenness in the mind of the addressee by the substance of its word. And then its use in an external individual, ambiguous or specified, like 'if you meet Usamah then flee from him, and this is Usamah approaching', is only from the aspect of the individual matching the essence, i.e. its truthfulness upon it from the aspect that it is not it, from the aspect of its givenness in the mind of the addressee considered in the genus proper noun. So its use in the individual absolutely is metaphorical as Ibn al-Hajib and al-Radi stated, and our teacher Sayyidi al-Tayyib followed them in his glosses on [something], not literal as al-Sa'd and al-Mahalli following him imagined, because individuals entail the essence per se, not from the aspect of presence which is the meaning of definition. Then he said in the chapter on investigations of words: with consideration of its existence in its external individuals, and therefore the first is particular and the second is universal. His saying: (with consideration of its existence in its external individuals) i.e. so the genus noun is posited for the essence as one unspecified unit, called an ambiguous individual, a spreading individual, and a common unit. This is the statement of al-Amidi, Ibn al-Hajib, al-Subki and Sa'd al-Din. And it was said: the genus noun is posited for the essence per se, and its use in the individual is only for the realization of the essence in it and its being an instance of it, and it is a literal not metaphorical use because the word is used in the essence, and individuality is derived externally. So the distinction between the genus proper noun and the genus noun on the first statement is from two aspects: one: that the genus proper noun is posited for the essence while disregarding its external referents, and the genus noun is posited for it with the condition of its existence in one unspecified individual, and that is from the referents. Second: that the genus proper noun indicates by the substance of its word that that essence is known in the mind of the addressee, present in it, conceptualized to him, and the genus noun does not indicate any givenness at all. As for on the second statement, it is from one aspect: that both, although posited for the essence disregarding its individuals, yet in the genus proper noun there is an additional condition: the indication by the substance of its word that that essence is known and known to the addressee, and the genus noun does not indicate that except by the article if it exists. The disagreement is only concerning the subject of the indefinite genus noun; as for the one defined by the lām of essence, it is equal in meaning to the genus proper noun. All this is when we say the genus proper noun is definite in word and meaning. But if we say it is definite in word only, then it is synonymous in meaning to the genus noun as Ibn Malik and al-Radi say, and then it is among universals. And to the mentioned distinction between the genus proper noun and the genus noun I alluded in my saying: When you want the distinction between the genus proper noun and its name, verify and understand. So the proper noun is the essence present in the mind, and pay attention to the individual if you consider it. And the noun is what is posited for the essence with the condition of singularity, so this is its way. And it was said: the noun is for the essence per se, however it may be essence, and the individual is not considered in it. And the first view is what the people of consideration verified.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and comparative analysis from a commentary on al-Sullam al-Munawraq. It addresses the distinction between two types of proper nouns: the 'alam al-jins (genus proper noun) and ism al-jins (genus noun). The passage opens by defining two categories of nouns that denote particularized entities: the first is particularized in external reality (like 'Zayd' and 'Mecca'), and the second is particularized in the mind (like 'Usamah' and 'Abu al-Harith' for the lion). The author then notes scholarly disagreement on the distinction between the second type (the mental proper noun, i.e., 'alam al-jins) and the ordinary genus noun (ism al-jins) like 'asad' (lion). The chosen view is that of Ibn Khatima: 'alam al-jins is posited for the essence itself, disregarding its existence in external individuals, while ism al-jins is posited for the essence with consideration of its existence in individuals. Hence the first is particular (because it points to a specific real entity, even if in the mind?) Wait, the text says the first (alam jins) is particular and the second (ism jins) is universal. This is because, as the commentator explains, a relative particular (like 'alam jins) can be universal in concept, whereas a real particular cannot. The commentator then reinforces that the differentia of 'alam jins is that it is posited without any restriction—neither specifying a real external individual nor an individual in the mind—while ism jins considers existence in a non-specific individual. The passage continues with a detailed elaborations, contrasting the views of different scholars: on one view, ism jins is posited for the essence as one unspecified individual (like 'a man'), while on another view it is posited for the essence per se and its use for individuals is figurative. The commentator then lists two points of difference between 'alam jins and ism jins on the first view, and one point on the second view. Finally, the commentator presents a poetic summary of the main distinction. Throughout, the passage uses examples from language (like 'Usamah' for lion, 'Bayt' for the Kaaba) to illustrate how these nouns function in Arabic.

Classifying Names Like Book Titles as 'Alam Jins
Classification of names like pronouns and book titles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify names like book titles as 'alam jins and distinguish them from 'alam shakhs and common nouns based on the criteria discussed.

Core Idea
Names like book titles are 'alam jins: they name a mental reality, not a specific individual.

Is a book title like 'Tashil al-Fawa'id' a proper name for a specific copy or a genus-name for any copy? This passage presents an objection that such names are used for specific individuals, but the author resolves that they are 'alam jins—placed for the mental reality of the kind, not for individuals. Let's see how.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection states that names placed for general specificities (like pronouns and book titles) are mostly used for specific individuals. For example, 'al-damir' (the pronoun) is used for a particular pronoun, and book titles are used for what is common among individuals, not the specific copy.
The objector is Abu al-Abbas al-Hilali.
2
Extract the preferred view
The author's preferred view is that such names are 'alam jins (proper names of genus). The coiner considered one type of content (e.g., the specific composition of the book) and placed the name for it while disregarding individuals.
'Alam jins differs from 'alam shakhs (proper name of a specific individual).
3
Follow the commentary's explanation
The commentator explains that a universal, when considered without individuals, becomes mentally individuated—one thing. So the name is truly a proper name of that mental reality. Example: The author (Ibn Malik) placed 'Tashil al-Fawa'id' for the composition with a specific form, disregarding the utterer.
4
Contrast with the rejected third opinion
Some said they are common nouns (asma' al-ajnas). This is rejected because such names are not used as indefinites (except for 'Quran' in one sense). For example, 'Quran' can be indefinite (any part of the book) or definite (the whole book). The definite use is under discussion.
The indefinite usage is not the topic here.
5
Note the final critique on literal use
The commentator notes that using a 'alam jins for a specific individual is metaphorical, not literal, as stated by al-Radi and Ibn al-Hajib. This counters the claim that 'placing the name for the mental reality does not contradict its being used truly for individuals'.

And an objection was raised against it: that a name placed for specificities with a general placement, like 'the pronoun', is mostly used for the specific individual from among them in terms of its being specific, and names of books are mostly used in what the mind conceives as common among their individuals, not in the specific individual of them. His statement: (And an objection was raised) The one who raised this objection is the scholar Abu al-Abbas al-Hilali, he said: 'I have a discussion about it.' His statement: (in what the mind conceives as common ... etc.) like: 'The Quran is the noblest of books', and 'al-Mukhtasar is more comprehensive than al-Risala', and 'Banat Su'ad is shorter than al-Burda', and so on ad infinitum.
His statement: (And the preferred view: that they are of the type of proper name of genus) Its explanation: that the universal matter, when one disregards its individuals and observes its reality as such, becomes one thing with no multiplicity, mentally individuated. So the name placed with this consideration is truly a proper name of genus, e.g., it is said that Ibn Malik placed 'Tashil al-Fawa'id' for the composition characterized by the specific form after individuating that in his mind, disregarding the utterer, to distinguish it thereby from other compositions.
Then this commentator did not mention the third opinion: that they are of the type of genus-names (asma' al-ajnas), due to its unsoundness; because it is refuted by their not being used as indefinite except for 'Quran', for it has two uses: indefinite use: it applies to every part of the Noble Book that it is Quran, and it is then a genus‑name without doubt, and this is not the topic of discussion. And definite use: it is not applied except to the entire book from the start of al-Fatiha to the end of Surat al-Nas, and this is what is under investigation.
His statement: (does not contradict its being used truly) it is questionable; because of what we have previously stated: that the use of proper name of genus for the individual is always metaphorical, as stated by al-Radi and Ibn al-Hajib, and that is the truth.

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and the author's preferred resolution regarding the classification of certain names. The objection states that names placed for specific meanings with a general placement, like the pronoun 'al-damir', are typically used for a specific individual, whereas names of books (e.g., 'Tashil al-Fawa'id') are used for what the mind conceives as common among individuals, not for a specific individual. The author then gives the preferred view: such names are of the type 'alam jins (proper name of genus). The coiner considered one kind of accident and placed the name for it while disregarding individuals. The author further argues that placing the name for the mental reality does not preclude its being truly used for individuals, because the reality is inherent in them. In the margin commentary, the source of the objection is identified as Abu al-Abbas al-Hilali, and examples of such usage are given, like 'Quran', 'al-Mukhtasar', and 'Banat Su'ad'. The commentator explains that a universal matter, when observed as such, becomes mentally individuated, so the name is truly a proper name of genus. The commentator also notes that the third opinion (that they are genus-names like 'asma' al-ajnas') is rejected because such names are not used as indefinites except for 'Quran'. The commentator critiques the claim that using 'alam jins for individuals is literal, insisting it is metaphorical, citing al-Radi and Ibn al-Hajib.

Two Interpretations of Science Names: Rules vs. Faculty
Author distinguishes between names of sciences as proper names for rules or as 'alam jins for the faculty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two interpretations of names of Islamic sciences (e.g., al-mantiq, al-nahw) — either as proper names for the set of rules (a'lam ashkhas) or as proper names of genus for the faculty (alam jins) — and determine which interpretation applies in a given context.

Core Idea
The name of a science can refer either to its unique set of rules or to the universal faculty of mastering it.

In Islamic logic and other sciences, there is a dispute about whether names like 'al-mantiq' and 'al-nahw' are proper names of individuals (a'lam ashkhas) or proper names of genus (alam jins). The author resolves this by showing that both interpretations are valid depending on what is meant: the specific rules or the mental faculty. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly defining these sciences and avoiding confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations
The passage states that if the name refers to the specific rules (al-qawa'id al-makhsusa), it is a proper name of an individual (alam shakhs). If it refers to the perception (idrak) or faculty (malaka), it is a proper name of genus (alam jins).
2
Understand why the set of rules is considered a single individual
Because the totality of rules is one thing with no multiplicity; only the expressions and perceptions are multiple.
3
Understand why the faculty is a genus
Because the faculty is an accident that can have multiple instances (e.g., different people having the faculty), so it fits the category of alam jins.
4
Apply the distinction
Given a statement like 'I have mastered al-nahw,' determine which interpretation is intended based on context.

Source Text

I
And similarly, there is also a disagreement regarding the names of sciences, such as 'al-mantiq' and 'al-nahw' for example. And the truth: that if what is meant by them is the specific rules, then they are proper names of individuals (a'lam ashkhas); because the totality of those rules is one thing with no multiplicity, only the expressions indicating them are multiple. And if what is meant by them is the perception or the faculty, then they are of the type of proper name of genus ('alam jins).
[Margin]
His statement: (only the expressions indicating them are multiple) i.e., and the perceptions related to them, just as the names of a single person are multiple and his conception in the mind of Zayd, 'Amr, and others is multiple.
His statement: (And if what is meant by them is the perception or the faculty, then they are of the type of proper name of genus) because their meanings then are accidents whose individuals multiply, so consideration of individuation cannot be achieved in them.
And that they are of the type of proper name of genus is what al-Sayyid, al-'Abbadi, and others have verified.
And the scholar of the ummah, my master al-Hasan al-Yusi, investigated it, with the summary: that their being proper names is refuted by their definition; for definition is only for universal concepts, and the particular proper name is not definable because, as mentioned, particulars are not defined. His student, the investigator Ibn Zakari, transmitted his full words in his commentary on 'al-Farida'. And some investigators answered this investigation with the summary: that the proper name of genus is considered from two aspects: 1. from the aspect of its mental presence, and from this aspect its definition cannot be achieved. 2. And it is considered not from the aspect of its mental presence but from its essence as such, and with this consideration it is a universal thing and thus defined. So if you are asked: 'What is al-mantiq?' the answer does not come from the first aspect, because he is ignorant, so the situation compels that he be answered with the essence as such, and when it is present in the mind of the hearer, you point to it from the aspect of its presence in his mind and say to him: 'This is al-mantiq.' End.
•
And Ibn Abi Sharif, al-'Abbadi, and Ibn Zakari have spoken on the issue in the commentary on 'al-Farida', and he extended to about four folios, so look at it if you wish.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage resolves the dispute about whether names of sciences like 'al-mantiq' and 'al-nahw' are proper names of individuals (a'lam ashkhas) or proper names of genus (alam jins). The author states the truth: if what is meant by them is the specific set of rules (qawa'id makhsusa), then they are a'lam ashkhas because that set is a single entity with no multiplicity; only the expressions referring to it are multiple. But if what is meant is the perception (idrak) or the faculty (malaka) of that science, then they are from the type of alam jins, because these are accidents with multiple individuals. The margin commentary explains that the multiplicity of expressions and perceptions does not affect the singularity of the set of rules. It also cites al-Sayyid and al-'Abbadi verifying the second view. A critical investigation by al-Hasan al-Yusi raises the objection that if these names are proper names (a'lam), they cannot be defined, because definition applies only to universals. The response is that alam jins can be considered from two aspects: as mental presence (in which case it cannot be defined) and as an essence (which is universal and definable). The commentator suggests referring to longer discussions by Ibn Abi Sharif and others.

أعلام أصخاص
الملكة
التعريف
علم الجنس

C) Ism jins
D) Ism 'alam

Key Takeaway
Science names can be either proper names for the rules (a'lam ashkhas) or proper names of genus for the faculty (alam jins), depending on what is intended.

?
2. In a textbook, the author defines 'al-mantiq' as 'the instrument that safeguards the mind from error.' Which interpretation (rules or faculty) does this definition align with? Justify your answer.

Defining Alam Jins: The Two Aspects Solution
The objection by al-Yusi and the response about defining alam jins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two aspects of alam jins (mental presence vs. essence) and how they resolve the problem of defining proper names of genus in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Alam jins is indefinable as a mental particular but definable as a universal essence.

Al-Yusi raised a powerful objection: if science names are proper names (a'lam), they cannot be defined because definition applies only to universals. The response ingeniously shows that alam jins can be considered from two aspects — as mental presence (particular) and as essence (universal) — allowing it to be defined from the latter aspect. This lesson unpacks that resolution.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Yusi's objection
Al-Yusi argues that if science names like 'al-mantiq' are proper names (a'lam), they are particulars, and particulars cannot be defined because definition (ta'rif) only applies to universals.
2
Identify the two aspects of alam jins
The response states that alam jins can be considered from the aspect of mental presence (hudhur dhihni) — in which it is particular and indefinable — and from the aspect of its essence (dhat) — in which it is universal and definable.
3
See how this answers the objection
When someone asks 'What is al-mantiq?', they are asking for a definition of the essence, not the mental presence. So the answer can be given as a definition of the universal concept.
4
Apply this distinction to a concrete example
Consider the name 'al-nahw'. If a student has no concept of it, you define it by its essence (e.g., 'the science of Arabic grammar rules'). Once they understand, you can point to that concept and say 'This is al-nahw'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

٢ - ويلاحظ لا من جهة حضوره الذهني، بل من حيث هو هو، وهو بهذا الاعتبار يكون أمراً كليا فيعرف، فإذا قيل لك: «ما المنطق؟» لم يأتِ الجواب بالحيثيَّة الأولى؛ لأنَّه جاهل فألجأ به ، الحال إلى أن يُجاب بالماهية من حيث هي فإذا حضرت في ذهن السَّامع أشرت إليه من حيث
